line=22256 tag=M:        As brie y discussed in 10.1.1 above, this has also been noted for Russian, e.g., by Babby 1980a cf. also
line=22257 tag=M:    16
line=22258 tag=B:
line=22259 tag=M:  Timberlake 1975, Babby 1980b, fn.2, Babby 1986, fn.43, Fowler 1987, pp.307f., who claims that in
line=22260 tag=M:  Russian
line=22261 tag=M:  the only reason that sub jects, direct ob jects, and time adverbs are marked genitive under negation
line=22262 tag=M:  is that they do not happen to be marked by an oblique case p.86, see also p.150.
line=22263 tag=M:        Actually, Willim 1990, p.211 and Ta jsner 1990, p.246 deny that adjuncts can undergo GoN. On the
line=22264 tag=M:     17
line=22265 tag=B:
line=22266 tag=M:  other hand, Holvoet 1991, p.85 and Franks and Dziwirek 1993 consider such examples grammatical. We
line=22267 tag=M:  are not sure if this is the result of a genuine variation, or whether Willim's and Ta jsner's judgements stem from
line=22268 tag=M:  the fact that additional presuppositions are connected with the genitive variant, pace Holvoet 1991, p.85,
line=22269 tag=M:  or that they may have partitive meaning, pace Franks and Dziwirek 1993. In any case, all our informants
line=22270 tag=M:  considered both possibilities fully acceptable.
